You say also, [using the pass. form,] <foreign lang="ar">رِيعَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يُرَاعُ</foreign>, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَوْعٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, frightened,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">afraid;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he feared;</hi> (S, * K, * TA;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17078-2" target="ارتاع" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17078-3" target="تروّع" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n17078"/></foreign>. (S, K, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَاعَ مِنْهُ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَرُوعُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَوْعٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, frightened at it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">afraid of it;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he feared it.</hi> (TK. [But I know of no authority on which this is founded, except a prov. (cited in art. <foreign lang="ar">جعر</foreign>) , in which some read <foreign lang="ar">رُوعِى جَعَارِ</foreign> instead of <foreign lang="ar">رُوغِى</foreign>.]) To a man, you say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا تُرَعْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Be not thou frightened;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">fear not thou; let not fear overtake thee:</hi> and to a woman, <foreign lang="ar">لَا تُرَاعِى</foreign>. (S, TA.) And hence the saying, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَنْ تُرَاعَوْا مَا رَأَيْنَا مِنْ شَىْءٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Ye shall not be frightened,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">afraid: we saw not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have not seen, anything</hi>]. (TA.) You also say, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17078-4" target="ارتاع" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مِنْهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, frightened at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">afraid of, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he feared him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">It affected his</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُوع</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">heart,</hi> or <pb n="1188"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">mind, with a sudden surprise; it took him by surprise.</hi>] One says, <foreign lang="ar">مَا رَاعَنِى إِلَّا مَجِيؤُكَ</foreign> meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Nothing took me by surprise but thy coming;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">I was surprised by thy coming;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">I knew not save thy coming;</hi> as though he said, <hi rend="ital">nothing struck my</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُوع</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">but thy coming.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجْتُ وَ مَا رَاعَنِى إِلَّا فُلَانٌ لِالبَابِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">I went forth, and nothing took me by surprise but such a one at the door</hi>]; which is equivalent to saying, <hi rend="ital">and lo, such a one was at the door.</hi> (Har p. 207.) And it is said in a trad. of I'Ab, <foreign lang="ar">فَلَمْ يَرُعْنِى إِلَّا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ آخِذٌ بِمَنْكِبِى</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">I knew not</hi> [<hi rend="ital">save a man taking hold of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seizing, my shoulder-joint</hi>]; as though he came upon him suddenly, or unexpectedly, without any previous appointment, and without knowledge, and so that event frightened him. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [<hi rend="ital">It affected his</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُوع</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">heart,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mind, with admiration,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pleasure;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">it excited his admiration and approval; it pleased him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rejoiced him;</hi> (S, Msb, K;) said of beauty [&amp;c.]. (Msb.) It is said in a trad., describing the people of Paradise, <foreign lang="ar">فَيَرُوعُهُ مَا عَلَيْهِ مِنَ اللِّبَاسِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And what is upon him, of apparel, excites his admiration</hi> &amp;c., by its beauty. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [<hi rend="ital">It</hi> (drink) <hi rend="ital">cooled it,</hi> (namely, the heart,) or <hi rend="ital">allayed its thirst.</hi>] A poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">سَقَتْنِى شَرْبَةً رَاعَتْ فُؤَادِى</foreign>
                     </L>

                        <foreign lang="ar">سَقَاهَا ٱللّٰهُ مِنْ حَوْضِ الرَّسُولِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">She gave me to drink a draught that cooled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">allayed the thirst of, my heart: may God give her to drink from the pool of the Apostle</hi> in Paradise]. (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذِهِ شَرْبَةٌ رَاعَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِهَا فُؤَادِى</foreign> [which may be rendered <hi rend="ital">This is a draught by which he has cooled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">allayed the thirst of, my heart;</hi> and it is implied in the TA that this is the right meaning: or it means] <hi rend="ital">this is a draught by which the thirst,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vehement thirst, of my heart has been allayed:</hi> (so accord. to the pointing in the copies of the K:) mentioned by Az. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  The verb from <foreign lang="ar">رَوَعٌ</foreign> [q. v. infrà] is one and the same [whether trans. or intrans.; i. e., you say <foreign lang="ar">رَاعَهُ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَرُوعُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَوْعٌ</foreign>, meaning “He,” or “it, excited his admiration and approval,” &amp;c., as expl. above; and <foreign lang="ar">رَاعَ</foreign>, app. with the same aor. and inf. n., meaning <hi rend="ital">He possessed the quality of exciting admiration and approval by his beauty and the pleasingness of his aspect,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by his courage,</hi> &amp;c.; and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">رَاعَتْ</foreign>, said of a woman]; the trans. verb [in this case] being like the trans. [in other cases], and the intrans. [in this case] like the intrans. [in other cases]: but the regular form, accord. to Az, of the [intrans.] verb hence derived is <foreign lang="ar">رَوِعَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَرْوَعُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَوَعٌ</foreign>. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَاعَ فِى يَدِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign>: see art. <foreign lang="ar">ريع</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">رَاعَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَرُوعُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">يَرِيعُ</foreign>, inf. n. of the former <foreign lang="ar">رُوَاعٌ</foreign>, and of the latter <foreign lang="ar">رَيْعٌ</foreign>: see art. <foreign lang="ar">ريع</foreign>.    </entryFree>28:T15bc,<entryFree id="n17079" key="رَوْعٌ" type="main">

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17079-1" target="رَوعٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [accord. to some, but this seems to be little known]. (TA.) Hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَ رَوْعُهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">His fright,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fear, departed.</hi> (S.) Az says, All the lexicologists whom I have met say <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَ رَوْعُهُ</foreign>, with fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ر</foreign> [in <foreign lang="ar">روعه</foreign>], except El-Mundhiree, who informs me that AHeyth used to say, It is only   
      <foreign lang="ar">افرخ <ref cref="n17079-2" target="رَوْعُكَ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, with damm. (TA.) Accord. to different relations of a trad., you say,   
      <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَ <ref cref="n17079-3" target="رُوعُكَ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Fright,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fear, hath departed from thy heart;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">may fright,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fear, depart from thy heart;</hi> (K, TA;) thus expl. by AHeyth; (TA;) and <foreign lang="ar">افرخ رَوْعُكَ</foreign>, with fet-h; or this latter, only, is the right, and means <hi rend="ital">what thou fearest hath quitted thee, and departed from thee, and become removed;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">may what thou fearest quit thee,</hi> &amp;c.; as though it were taken from the young bird's going forth from the egg, (K, TA,) and the darkness' becoming removed from it; thus expl. by Aboo-Ahmad El-Hasan Ibn-' Abd-Allah Ibn-Sa'eed El-' Askeree; and AO says that <foreign lang="ar">افرخ روعك</foreign> [thus in the TA, without any syll. signs,] means <hi rend="ital">let thy fright,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fear, depart,</hi> for the case is not as thou fearest it to be. (TA.) It is also said, in a trad. of Mo'áwiyeh, that he wrote in a letter to Ziyád,   
      <foreign lang="ar">لِيُفْرِخْ <ref cref="n17079-4" target="رُوعُكَ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, with damm; (K, TA;) but the opinion commonly obtaining with the leading lexicologists is, that it is with fet-h; except AHeyth, who relates it thus, with damm; (TA;) meaning <hi rend="ital">Dismiss thou the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَوْع</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">from thy</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُوع</foreign>; (K, TA;) i. e., <hi rend="ital">the fright,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fear, from thy heart:</hi> (TA:) for you say <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَتِ البَيْضَةُ</foreign> when the young bird quits the egg; and <foreign lang="ar">رَوْع</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">fright,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fear,</hi> which does not depart from itself, but from its place, which is the <foreign lang="ar">رُوع</foreign>, with damm; (AHeyth, K;) the <foreign lang="ar">رَوْع</foreign> in the <foreign lang="ar">رُوع</foreign> being like the young bird in the egg: in like manner also one says <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَ فُؤَادُ الرَّجُلِ</foreign> when a man's fright, or fear, departs: but Dhu-r-Rummeh, though knowing the meaning, has made an inversion, saying, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ أَفْرَخَتْ عَنْ رُوعِهِ الكُرَبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [for <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ أَفْرَخَ عَنِ الكُرَبِ رُوعُهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">His heart had freed itself from griefs</hi>]. (AHeyth, TA.) AHeyth adds, (TA,) one also says, <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرِخَ <ref cref="n17079-5" target="رُوعَكَ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَنِ الأَمْرِ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى الأَمْرِ</foreign>, [accord. to different copies of the K, the latter being the reading in the TA, but the former probably the right,] meaning [<hi rend="ital">Free thy heart from the affair;</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">be thou tranquil, and without fear.</hi> (K, TA.) Az observes, What AHeyth says is clear; but I am averse from it because of his being alone in his saying; though sometimes later authorities correct things in which the earlier have erred; therefore the correctness of AHeyth may not be [absolutely] denied in this matter, seeing that he had an ample share of knowledge. (TA.)
